Topic: Surgery
Question: Obstructive sleep apnoea caused by the following
Choices:
  A: Mandibular ameloblasma
  B: Dentigerous cyst
  C: Orbital fracture
  D: Bilateral TMJ ankylosis
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  A: Mandibular ameloblastoma is a locally invasive odontogenic tumor in the jaw, not related to sleep apnea.
  B: Dentigerous cyst is an odontogenic cyst associated with the crown of an unerupted tooth, not related to sleep apnea.
  C: Orbital fracture is a break in one or more bones that form the orbit, which could cause diplopia, enophthalmos, or other complications, but not sleep apnea.
  D: Bilateral temporomandibular joint (TMJ) ankylosis, which refers to fusion of the jawbone and the skull bone at the TMJ, may restrict mouth opening and interfere with normal breathing, leading to sleep apnea.
Action: Answer("D")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  A: Mandibular ameloblastoma is a benign odontogenic tumor that can expand and invade the surrounding tissues, but it does not cause obstructive sleep apnea.
  B: A dentigerous cyst is an odontogenic cyst that usually forms around the crown of an unerupted tooth. It does not cause obstructive sleep apnea.
  C: An orbital fracture occurs when one or more of the bones surrounding the eye are broken. It does not cause obstructive sleep apnea.
  D: Bilateral temporomandibular joint (TMJ) ankylosis, which is a condition where the TMJ joint is fused, can cause obstructive sleep apnea because it can obstruct the airway.
Action: Answer("D")
Response 2:

  B: Dentigerous cyst is a type of cyst that forms around an unerupted tooth. It may cause swelling and pain, but it is not known to cause obstructive sleep apnea.
  C: Orbital fracture is a break in one or more bones that make up the eye socket (orbit). It may cause swelling and pain around the eye, but it is not known to cause obstructive sleep apnea.
  D: Bilateral TMJ (temporomandibular joint) ankylosis refers to the fusion of the jawbone to the skull, which can cause difficulty in opening the mouth, speaking, and swallowing. It is known to cause obstructive sleep apnea.
Action: Answer("D")

Topic: Medicine
Question: A 60 years old patient who had myocardial infarction 2 weeks back, the lipid profile is done for a patient and reveals HDL 32 mgldL, LDL 126 mg/dl, TG 276 mgl/dL. Which of the following is preferred for this patient ?
Choices:
  A: Rosuvastatin + Fenofibrate
  B: Fenofibrate alone
  C: Rosuvastatin 10 mg
  D: Atorvastatin 80 mg
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  Myocardial infarction is a heart attack caused by a blockage in an artery supplying blood to the heart muscle, and the patient in this question had a heart attack 2 weeks ago.
  HDL, LDL, and TG are different types of cholesterol that make up a lipid profile.
  Rosuvastatin and atorvastatin are both statins, which are a class of medications used to lower cholesterol levels.
  Fenofibrate is a medication used to lower triglyceride levels.
 
Analysis:
  The patient's lipid profile shows high triglyceride levels and low HDL cholesterol levels, in addition to high LDL cholesterol levels. This profile indicates a higher risk for developing cardiovascular disease. Given that the patient recently had a heart attack, it is important to manage their cholesterol levels effectively to prevent future incidents. Fenofibrate appears to be a good option to help reduce the high triglyceride levels, but it is not the mainstay of therapy for cholesterol reduction. Both Rosuvastatin and Atorvastatin have proven efficacy for LDL reduction, however, the dose of Atorvastatin in this option is too high and is generally not recommended. Therefore, Rosuvastatin 10mg is the preferred option for this patient.

Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  High HDL levels are considered cardioprotective.
  High LDL levels and high triglyceride levels are considered risk factors for coronary artery disease.
  Statins are first-line treatment for high LDL.
  Fibrates are used to treat high triglycerides.
  Combining a statin and fibrate may increase the risk of myopathy/rhabdomyolysis.
  The maximum recommended dose of atorvastatin is 40 mg/day due to the risk of myopathy.
Action: Answer("C")  
Explanation: 
  Given the patient has a recent myocardial infarction and has borderline low HDL, high LDL, and high TG, a statin (such as rosuvastatin) would be the best medication to start with based on current guidelines. The goal of therapy will be to lower LDL and reduce the risk of cardiovascular events. Adding a fibrate would not be recommended at this time because fibrates are indicated when the primary lipid abnormality is high triglycerides. While there are combination products that contain a statin and a fibrate, the combination should be used with caution and only after careful consideration of the risks and benefits.
Response 2:
Knowledge:
  Myocardial infarction (MI) is commonly known as a heart attack, occurs when blood flow decreases or stops to a part of the heart, causing damage to heart muscle. 
  In general, the goal of treating hyperlipidemia after an MI is to reduce LDL cholesterol levels. 
  High-density lipoprotein (HDL) is protective against heart disease, while low-density lipoprotein (LDL) increases the risk.
  Triglycerides (TG) are a type of fat found in your blood. 
  Treatment of hyperlipidemia after an MI includes lifestyle modifications, such as weight loss, smoking cessation, increased physical activity, and medications.
  A: Rosuvastatin + Fenofibrate combination is preferred when both LDL and TG are high and HDL is low.
  B: Fenofibrate alone may be preferred when only TG are high.
  C: Rosuvastatin 10 mg may be preferred when only LDL is high.
  D: Atorvastatin 80 mg is a high dose, and it may be preferred when LDL is very high.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 3:
Knowledge:
  The patient had a myocardial infarction, which is a heart attack.
  The lipid profile of the patient reveals low HDL, high LDL, and high triglyceride levels. 
  A: Rosuvastatin + Fenofibrate is a combination medication that helps in decreasing cholesterol levels in the blood. It is useful in cases where the patient has both high cholesterol and high triglycerides.
  B: Fenofibrate is a medication that helps to decrease triglycerides and increase HDL levels in the blood. It is useful in cases where the patient has only high triglycerides.
  C: Rosuvastatin is a medication that helps to decrease cholesterol levels in the blood. It is useful in cases where the patient has only high cholesterol.
  D: Atorvastatin is a medication that helps to decrease cholesterol levels in the blood. It is useful in cases where the patient has only high cholesterol.
  
Answer: 
  The patient has low HDL, high LDL, and high triglyceride levels. So, the best option would be a combination of medications that can target both high cholesterol and high triglycerides which is Rosuvastatin + Fenofibrate. Hence, the answer is A. Answer("A")
Response 4:
Knowledge:
  High-density lipoprotein (HDL) is the "good" cholesterol that helps remove the "bad" low-density lipoprotein (LDL) or "bad" cholesterol from arteries.
  Low-density lipoprotein (LDL) is the "bad" cholesterol, which is considered a major contributor to atherosclerosis and heart disease.
  Triglycerides (TG) are a type of fat found in the blood that your body uses for energy.
  The patient had a myocardial infarction (heart attack) within the last two weeks.
Action: Answer("C") 
Explanation: 
  The patient had a recent heart attack, which requires careful management of cholesterol levels. 
  According to the American College of Cardiology/American Heart Association guidelines, statin therapy is preferred in most patients after a heart attack, regardless of their initial cholesterol levels. 
  Rosuvastatin is a high-intensity statin that is appropriate for this patient and can decrease LDL levels by 50% or more. 
  Fenofibrate is a fibric acid derivative that can decrease triglyceride levels, but it has not been shown to reduce cardiovascular events in patients with a history of heart attacks. 
  Combination therapy with a statin and fenofibrate may increase the risk of side effects, such as muscle damage or liver problems. 
  Atorvastatin is another high-intensity statin that can decrease LDL levels; however, a dose of 80 mg is generally reserved for patients who cannot achieve target LDL levels with lower doses.
Response 5:
Knowledge: 
  The patient had myocardial infarction two weeks back suggesting an acute coronary syndrome. This means the patient has coronary artery disease (CAD) which is caused by dyslipidemia (abnormal levels of lipids and/or lipoproteins) among other factors. 
  Target LDL levels for patients with CAD is less than 70 mg/dL or 1.8 mmol/L and target non-HDL-C levels for patients with CAD is less than 100 mg/dL or 2.6 mmol/L. 
  HDL levels of 60 mg/dL or more are considered protective. 
  Triglyceride levels of <150 mg/dL or 1.7 mmol/L are optimal, 150–199 mg/dL or 1.7–2.2 mmol/L are borderline high, 200–499 mg/dL or 2.3–5.6 mmol/L are high and levels >500 mg/dL or >5.6 mmol/L are very high.
  A: Rosuvastatin is known to lower LDL cholesterol levels, and fenofibrate is known to lower triglyceride levels and raise HDL cholesterol levels. However, this combination is not preferred due to increased risk of myopathy and rhabdomyolysis. Additionally, the patient's LDL level is only mildly elevated, and their HDL level is not extremely low.
  B: Fenofibrate alone is preferred in patients with high levels of triglycerides, which is the case in this patient, but it doesn't target the LDL level, which is mildly elevated in this patient and needs control to reduce the risk of further cardiovascular events.
  C: Rosuvastatin 10 mg is a good choice as it effectively lowers LDL cholesterol level, which is mildly elevated in this patient, and the patient's HDL level is not extremely low. Rosuvastatin has no significant effect on triglyceride levels, but in this patient, the triglyceride level is very high and needs control, which can be achieved by lifestyle modifications.
  D: Atorvastatin 80 mg is not preferred as it is associated with a higher risk of myopathy and rhabdomyolysis than other statins, such as rosuvastatin, and the patient's LDL level is only mildly elevated, and their HDL level is not extremely low.
Action: Answer("C")

Topic: Anatomy
Question: Which of the following structure is not present on floor of third ventricle?
Choices:
  A: Optic stalk
  B: Third nerve
  C: Infundibulum
  D: Mammillary body
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  The third ventricle is one of the four ventricles of the brain and is located in the midline, between the two thalami. 
  A: The optic stalk extends from the optic nerve to the optic chiasm, forming the roof of the optic recess in the third ventricle.
  B: The oculomotor nerve (third cranial nerve) arises from the midbrain and enters the third ventricle to supply the levator palpebrae superioris, superior rectus, inferior rectus, medial rectus, and inferior oblique muscles.
  C: The infundibulum (pituitary stalk) extends from the base of the hypothalamus to the posterior lobe of the pituitary gland. It is located at the midline of the floor of the third ventricle.
  D: The mammillary bodies are a pair of small round bodies located on the undersurface of the brain and are part of the limbic system. They are located posterior to the infundibulum and form the posterior border of the tuber cinereum. 
Action: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  The third ventricle is a cavity in the brain, located between the two thalami.
  A: Optic stalk is present on the floor of third ventricle.
  B: The third nerve is present in the midbrain, not on the floor of the third ventricle.
  C: Infundibulum is the stalk connecting the hypothalamus to the pituitary gland and it is located on the floor of third ventricle.
  D: Mammillary body is located on the floor of third ventricle.

  D: Mammillary body is present on the floor of the third ventricle.

Response 5:
Knowledge:
  The third ventricle is a cavity filled with cerebrospinal fluid (CSF) that is located in the midline of the brain, below the corpus callosum and above the brainstem. 
  The floor of the third ventricle contains several structures like optic chiasm, mamillary bodies, infundibulum, etc. 
  A: Optic stalk, also known as optic nerve, is a paired nerve that transmits visual information from the retina of the eye to the brain. It lies on the floor of the third ventricle.
  B: Third nerve, also known as oculomotor nerve, is one of the twelve cranial nerves. It supplies most of the muscles controlling eye movement and lies on the floor of the third ventricle.
  C: Infundibulum is a funnel-shaped structure that connects the hypothalamus of the brain to the pituitary gland. It is an important part of the hypothalamic-pituitary axis and it lies on the floor of the third ventricle.
  D: Mammillary body is a pair of small, round structures located on the undersurface of the brain, lying on the floor of the third ventricle.

Action: Answer("D")

Topic: Pediatrics
Question: Short child with low T4 and raised TSH and swelling of pituitary, what is the diangosis ?
Choices:
  A: Primary hypothyrodism
  B: Pituitary tumor
  C: TSH Secreting pituitary adenoma
  D: TSH resistance
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  T4 is thyroid hormone and TSH is thyroid-stimulating hormone.
  Low T4 and high TSH indicate hypothyroidism.
  A: Primary hypothyroidism is the most common cause of hypothyroidism and it happens when the thyroid gland does not produce enough thyroid hormone.
  B: Pituitary tumor can cause elevated hormone production but does not account for low T4 levels.
  C: TSH-secreting pituitary adenoma is a rare type of adenoma that produces excess TSH but does not account for the low T4 levels.
  D: TSH resistance is a rare genetic disorder that causes the thyroid gland to be less responsive to TSH, which leads to elevated TSH levels and normal to elevated levels of thyroid hormone.
Based on the symptoms mentioned in the question, the diagnosis is most likely a TSH-secreting pituitary adenoma.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  T4 is thyroxine, a hormone produced by the thyroid gland.
  TSH is thyroid-stimulating hormone, a hormone produced by the pituitary gland that stimulates the thyroid gland to produce T4.
  Primary hypothyroidism is a condition in which the thyroid gland does not produce enough thyroid hormone.
  A pituitary tumor can affect hormone production and regulation.
  TSH-secreting pituitary adenoma is a type of pituitary tumor that secretes excessive amounts of TSH.
  TSH resistance is a rare condition in which the thyroid gland is unable to respond to TSH, leading to decreased production of thyroid hormone.
  Swelling of the pituitary gland can be caused by a number of conditions, including tumors and inflammation.

Action: Answer("C") 
Based on the information given, the patient's low T4 and high TSH levels suggest primary hypothyroidism. However, the fact that there is swelling of the pituitary gland suggests that there may be a pituitary tumor present. The combination of elevated TSH and pituitary swelling suggests that the tumor is a TSH-secreting pituitary adenoma, which is the most likely diagnosis.
Response 2:
Knowledge:
- T4 is the thyroid hormone produced by the thyroid gland.
- TSH is the thyroid stimulating hormone produced by the pituitary gland.
- The pituitary gland is responsible for producing and secreting several hormones including TSH.
- Primary hypothyroidism is caused by an underactive thyroid gland.
- A pituitary tumor can cause an increase in TSH secretion.
- TSH-secreting pituitary adenomas are rare tumors that cause the pituitary gland to produce too much TSH.
- TSH resistance is a rare condition where the body is unable to respond to TSH.

Action: Answer("C")  
Based on the given information, the child has low T4 and raised TSH which indicate hypothyroidism. The swelling of pituitary suggests the presence of a pituitary adenoma. Since the pituitary adenoma is overproducing TSH, it leads to an increase in TSH level despite the low T4 level. So, the correct diagnosis is TSH-secreting pituitary adenoma.
Response 3:
Knowledge:
  T4 is thyroxine hormone which is produced by thyroid gland.
  TSH is thyroid stimulating hormone which is produced by pituitary gland.
  When T4 level is low, it causes negative feedback and pituitary gland produces more TSH.
  Pituitary gland can get swollen due to overactivity or due to the presence of a tumor.
  
Answer: "C" TSH secreting pituitary adenoma is the most likely diagnosis, as it can cause low T4, raised TSH and swelling of pituitary gland. Primary hypothyroidism can cause low T4, but TSH levels are higher than normal in that case. Pituitary tumor can cause raised TSH but it usually does not cause low T4 levels. TSH resistance usually presents with raised TSH levels but normal T4 levels.
Response 4:
Knowledge:
  T4 and TSH are hormones secreted by thyroid gland.
  Low T4 and high TSH are suggestive of hypothyroidism.
  Pituitary is a gland at the base of the brain that secretes hormones that regulate other hormones in the body.
  Pituitary swelling can occur due to various reasons, including pituitary tumors.
  TSH-secreting pituitary adenoma is a rare type of pituitary tumor that causes excessive production of TSH, leading to hyperthyroidism.
  TSH resistance is a rare genetic disorder in which the thyroid gland is less responsive to TSH, leading to elevated TSH and normal or slightly elevated thyroid hormone levels.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 5:
Knowledge:
  T4 and TSH are thyroid function tests.
  In primary hypothyroidism, T4 is low and TSH is high.
  Pituitary tumor can cause a variety of hormonal disturbances, including abnormal growth hormone release.
  TSH-secreting pituitary adenoma is rare but can cause hyperthyroidism.
  TSH resistance is a rare condition in which the thyroid gland is present and producing thyroid hormone, but the thyroid hormone levels in the blood are not affected appropriately by the TSH signal from the pituitary.

  C: A TSH secreting pituitary adenoma can cause hyperthyroidism and pituitary gland enlargement.
  D: TSH resistance is a very rare genetic disorder where there is resistance to the action of thyroid hormones.
  
Analysis:
  The given symptoms of a short child with low T4, raised TSH, and swelling of the pituitary are indicative of a pituitary gland problem affecting the regulation of thyroid hormones. Thus, the correct answer is likely to involve pituitary gland pathology. Option A, primary hypothyroidism, is incorrect since it suggests a problem with the thyroid gland itself. Option B, pituitary tumor, and Option C, TSH secreting pituitary adenoma, both involve abnormal functioning of the pituitary gland and could cause similar symptoms. Between the two, Option C is more specific as it mentions TSH secretion. Knowledge:
  Thyroid Stimulating Hormone (TSH) is released by the pituitary gland and stimulates the thyroid gland to release Thyroxine (T4) hormone.

Question: Which of following is an oral precancer?
Choices:

  B: White spongy naevus

  C: Leukemia is a type of blood cancer that does not have a direct relation to oral pathology.

Question: Naive T cell get activated by:
Choices:
  A: NK cell
  B: Dendritic cell
  C: Macrophage
  D: B-lymphocyte
Response 0:

  Naive T cells are mature T cells that have not been exposed to a specific antigen.

  Dendritic cells are professional antigen-presenting cells that are critical for activating naive T cells.
  Macrophages are also professional antigen-presenting cells and are capable of activating naive T cells.
  B-lymphocytes are not antigen-presenting cells. They produce antibodies in response to specific antigens.

  Naive T cell is a T cell that has not encountered its target antigen.
  A: NK cell (Natural Killer cell) is a type of cytotoxic lymphocyte that spontaneously kills cancer and virus-infected cells without prior exposure to antigen.
  B: Dendritic cells are antigen-presenting cells. They process antigen material and present it on the cell surface to T cells.
  C: Macrophages are white blood cells that play a role in the immune response by engulfing and digesting cellular debris and pathogens.
  D: B-lymphocytes are white blood cells that produce antibodies that bind to specific antigens.

Topic: Dental
Question: A lateral sliding flap done on a tooth with roots denuded for 6 years will show
Choices:
  A: PDL fibres attached to cementum
  B: PDL fibres attached to dentin
  C: Epithelium adjacent to previously denuded root surface
  D: Co adaptation to the remaining fibres
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  A lateral sliding flap is a dental procedure that involves making an incision in the gum tissue to expose the tooth root and underlying bone.
  The periodontal ligament (PDL) is a specialized connective tissue that surrounds the roots of teeth.
  Denudation is the loss of the outer layer of cementum and the exposing of dentin.
  
  A: PDL fibres attach to the cementum covering the root of the tooth, and could potentially be exposed if the cementum is denuded.
  B: PDL fibres are not attached to the dentin surface, but they do run perpendicular to the surface of the cementum.
  C: Epithelial cells cover the surface of the gingiva and can migrate along the root surface after denudation has occurred.
  D: Co adaptation occurs when a tooth is extracted and the PDL fibers are compressed.

Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  A lateral sliding flap is a surgical procedure in dentistry that involves a sliding flap of gingiva or gum tissue.
  The periodontal ligament (PDL) is a thin layer of tissue that surrounds the tooth root and helps keep the tooth in place.
  Root denudation is the exposure of the tooth root surface (the part of the tooth that is normally covered by gum tissue).
  
Option A: PDL fibres are typically attached to the cementum, which is a layer of hard tissue that covers the tooth root. However, given that the roots have been denuded for 6 years, it is not certain that PDL fibres would still be attached to the cementum.
Option B: PDL fibres may still be attached to the dentin, which is the hard tissue that makes up most of the tooth.
Option C: It is possible that epithelial cells (which make up the outermost layer of skin and mucous membranes) could have grown onto the previously denuded root surface.
Option D: Co-adaptation refers to the way in which different types of fibers in the PDL work together to help keep the tooth in place. However, it is not clear how the remaining PDL fibers would have adapted in a situation where the roots have been denuded.

Answer: Option B: PDL fibres attached to dentin.
Response 2:
Knowledge: 
  Lateral sliding flap surgery is a technique used to access the root surface of a tooth for treatment.
  In teeth with denuded roots, the periodontal ligament (PDL) fibers are lost and the root surface is covered by cementum, which is a calcified tissue covering the root surface of teeth.
  
A: PDL fibers attach to the cementum of the tooth root. This attachment is usually lost when the root surface is denuded.
B: PDL fibers do not attach to dentin, although the cementum is attached to dentin. 
C: Epithelium may grow over the previously denuded root surface, particularly if the root surface has not been covered by a soft tissue graft.
D: Adaptation of the remaining fibers is possible when there is some remaining attachment of the PDL fibers.

Action: Answer("A")
Response 3:
Knowledge: 
  A lateral sliding flap is a surgical procedure used to gain access to a tooth root while preserving the attached gingiva.
  Denuded roots are roots that have been stripped of their protective covering of cementum and periodontal ligament (PDL).
  A: If PDL fibers are attached to cementum, then it suggests the cementum is still present and the PDL has not been extensively damaged or lost due to the denuding process.
  B: If PDL fibers are attached to dentin, then it suggests the cementum has been lost and the PDL has attached itself directly to the dentin.
  C: The presence of epithelium adjacent to a previously denuded root surface suggests that the denuded area has not been properly covered or protected by the surgical flap.
  D: Co adaptation to the remaining fibers suggests proper healing and adaptation of the PDL fibers to the remaining cementum or dentin.
Action: Answer("B")

Choices:
  A: The PDL fibers would have been lost because of root denudation. Thus, they would not be attached to the cementum.
  B: The PDL fibers would have been lost because of root denudation. Thus, they would not be attached to the dentin.
  C: The long junctional epithelium would have formed adjacent to the previously denuded root surface.
  D: There would not be any co-adaptation to the remaining fibers in a tooth that has been root denuded for 6 years.

Action: Answer("C")
Response 8:
Knowledge:
  A lateral sliding flap is a surgical technique used in periodontal surgeries.
  In teeth with advanced periodontal disease, root surfaces may become exposed or denuded.
  PDL stands for periodontal ligament, which is a layer of connective tissue that connects the tooth root to the surrounding bone.
  A: PDL fibers normally attach the tooth root to the bone via cementum. If PDL fibers are still attached to the previously denuded cementum, it suggests that the tooth is still viable.
  B: If PDL fibers attach to the dentin, which is normally covered by cementum, it suggests that there has been some root resorption and the tooth may not be viable.
  C: The presence of epithelium adjacent to previously denuded root surface is expected in a healing tooth.
  D: Co adaptation to the remaining fibers, refers to the ability of periodontal fibers to reorient themselves and adapt to new stress in order to maintain stability.
  
Action: Answer("A")
Response 9:
Knowledge:
  1. A lateral sliding flap is a surgical technique used to access the root surface of a tooth.
  2. The periodontal ligament (PDL) is a group of fibers that connect the tooth to the surrounding alveolar bone.
  3. Root denudation occurs when the PDL fibers and the cementum which attaches it to the tooth surface are lost.
  
Answer: 
Based on the given information, the correct answer is C: Epithelium adjacent to the previously denuded root surface. 
Explanation: When PDL fibers and cementum are lost--as indicated in the question stem--the tooth surfaces become rough and fibrous, and the PDL fibers will attempt to re-attach to the tooth surface; however, the attachment will be done to the adjacent epithelium and not to the tooth surfaces.

Question: Which of the following has least density?
Choices:
  A: VLDL
  B: LDL
  C: HDL
  D: Chylomicrons
Response 0:

  A: VLDL stands for Very Low Density Lipoprotein. It contains more triglycerides and less protein than LDL.
  B: LDL stands for Low Density Lipoprotein. It contains more cholesterol and less protein than HDL.
  C: HDL stands for High Density Lipoprotein. It contains more protein and less cholesterol than LDL.
  D: Chylomicrons are lipoprotein particles that consist of dietary lipids and are responsible for transport of dietary lipids to the liver.
  
Since density is inversely related to the size of the lipoprotein particle, and chylomicrons are the largest of these lipoproteins, they would have the least density.
Action: Answer("D")
Response 1:
Knowledge: 
  A: VLDL or Very Low-Density Lipoproteins are produced in the liver and contain mostly triglycerides and cholesterol. These are the densest of all lipoproteins.

  C: HDL or High-Density Lipoproteins transport excess cholesterol from the cells to the liver for processing. These are the densest of all lipoproteins.
  D: Chylomicrons are formed in the small intestine after the consumption of fats. These are the least dense of all lipoproteins.

  A: 0
  B: 3
  C: 5
  D: 8
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  The Bishop score is used to assess the readiness of the cervix before induction of labor. The score includes cervical dilation, effacement, cervical consistency, fetal station, and cervical position. A Bishop score of 8 or more indicates that the cervix is favorable for induction of labor.
  In this case, the cervical dilation is 1 cm, effaced 30%, veex is at --1 station, and the cervix is soft and posterior. 
  The Bishop score is calculated as the sum of the individual scores assigned to each parameter. 
  The possible score ranges from 0 to 13.

Calculation: 
  Cervical dilation score: 1 cm = 0 points.
  Effacement score: 30% = 0 points.
  Cervical consistency score: Soft = 2 points.
  Fetal station score: --1 = 0 points.
  Cervical position score: Posterior = 0 points.

The modified Bishop score for this lady is 2.

  In a diabetic mother, fetal lungs tend to mature more slowly than in non-diabetic mothers. Amniocentesis can be performed to assess fetal lung maturity.
  A: L:S Ratio (Lecithin/Sphingomyelin) is an older test for fetal lung maturity. It is less commonly used now.
  B: Lecithin-Cephalin Ratio was used to assess fetal lung maturity before the L:S ratio. It is even less commonly used now.
  C: Phosphatidyl Choline is a type of lung surfactant that is produced by Type II pneumocytes in the lungs. It is one of the components of amniotic fluid.
  D: Phosphatidyl Glycerol is another type of lung surfactant that is produced by Type II pneumocytes in the lungs. It is one of the components of amniotic fluid.
  
Action: Answer("D")
Response 1:

- In diabetic mothers, fetal immaturity is commonly seen.
- Assessment of fetal lung maturity is an important aspect of the management of the diabetic mother.
- Lecithin-Sphingomyelin (L/S) ratio, Phosphatidyl glycerol (PG), and Foam stability index(FSI) are used for assessing fetal lung maturity.
- Out of these only L/S ratio and PG are widely used.
- L/S ratio and PG are the components of the surfactant, which is produced by type 2 alveolar cells and is necessary for the proper functioning of lungs.
- Lecithin-cephalin ratio and Phosphatidyl choline are old terminologies which have been replaced by L/S ratio and PG.

  B: Intravenous administration in emergency and urgent dosing
  C: Long half-life permits altemate day dosing

  It is obtained from the leaves of the foxglove plant (Digitalis lanata).
  The half-life of a drug is the time it takes for half of the drug to be eliminated from the body.

B: Intravenous administration may be used in emergency situations, but the half-life of the drug is not inherently related to this choice.
C: Correct. The long half-life of Digoxin permits alternate day dosing. Adjusting the dosing schedule is important for a patient's management of their heart condition.

Question: Multi constricted apical constriction is seen in which type of Dummer’s classification

  B: Type 2
  C: Type 3
  D: Type 4
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  Dummer's classification is a classification system used to describe the morphology of root canals.
  Type 1: A single, straight root canal from pulp chamber to apex
  Type 2: Two separate canals leaving the pulp chamber but merging short of the apex to form one canal
  Type 3: Two separate and distinct canals extend the entire length of the tooth
  Type 4: Multiple canals or canals with branches throughout the entire length of the tooth

Topic: Dental
Question: Sealants are effective in
Choices:
  A: Initial caries
  B: Secondary caries
  C: Recurrent caries
  D: Rampant caries
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  Sealants are thin, plastic coatings that are applied to the chewing surfaces of teeth, especially molars, to help prevent tooth decay. 
  A: Initial caries refers to the early stage of tooth decay, which is reversible.
  B: Secondary caries refers to tooth decay that occurs in the same tooth next to an existing filling or crown.
  C: Recurrent caries refers to tooth decay that occurs under a filling or crown.

Question: Object permanence seen in which stage of Jean Piaget’s theory
Choices:
  A: Sensorimotor
  B: Pre-operational stage
  C: Concrete operations stage
  D: Formal operations stage
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  Object permanence is the understanding that objects continue to exist even when they are no longer visible.
  Jean Piaget’s theory of cognitive development includes four stages: sensorimotor, pre-operational, concrete operations, and formal operations.
  Object permanence is developed in the sensorimotor stage which occurs from birth to about 2 years of age.

Response 2:
Knowledge:
  Jean Piaget is known for his theory on cognitive development which includes 4 stages: Sensorimotor stage, Pre-operational stage, Concrete operations stage and Formal operations stage.

  Object permanence is the understanding that objects continue to exist even when they cannot be seen, heard, or touched.

Action: Answer("A")  
Response 3:
Knowledge:
  Jean Piaget's theory of cognitive development consists of four main stages: 
  1. Sensorimotor stage (0-2 years): Object permanence is developed in this stage, which is the understanding that an object still exists even if it cannot be seen or sensed.
  2. Pre-operational stage (2-7 years): Children in this stage are egocentric, have difficulty understanding the perspective of others and their thinking is not yet logical.
  3. Concrete operational stage (7-12 years): Children begin to think logically and understand concrete events, e.g. conservation of mass, volume and number.
  4. Formal operational stage (12+ years): Children develop abstract thinking and can understand hypothetical situations.

Knowledge:
  Jean Piaget was a Swiss psychologist who proposed a theory of cognitive development. 
  The theory suggests that cognitive development occurs in stages, and each stage is characterized by a particular way of thinking.
  Object permanence is the understanding that objects continue to exist even when they cannot be seen, heard, or touched.
  A: Sensorimotor is the first stage in Piaget's theory, which lasts from birth to around 2 years old. Children during this stage learn through their five senses and by interacting with the environment around them. Object permanence is a major developmental milestone in this stage.
  B: Pre-operational stage is the second stage in Piaget's theory, which lasts from around 2 to 7 years old. Children during this stage develop more complex ways of thinking and learn to use symbols, such as words and numbers. However, they still struggle with the concept of object permanence.
  C: Concrete operations stage is the third stage in Piaget's theory, which lasts from around 7 to 11 years old. Children during this stage begin to think logically and understand the concept of object permanence.
  D: Formal operations stage is the fourth and final stage in Piaget's theory, which lasts from around 11 years old to adulthood. Adolescents during this stage develop abstract thinking abilities and can reason hypothetically.

Topic: Physiology
Question: Which of the following is rapid source of energy by resynthesizing ATP for exercising muscles is?
Choices:
  A: Glycolysis
  B: Glycogenolysis
  C: TCA cycle
  D: Phosphocreatine
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  To provide energy during physical activity, our body can use ATP (Adenosine Triphosphate) stored in the muscles.
  Phosphocreatine is used to resynthesize ATP quickly in exercising muscles.
  Glycolysis, Glycogenolysis, and TCA cycle are involved in the production of ATP but not as a rapid source of energy.
Action: Answer("D")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  A: Glycolysis is the breakdown of glucose into pyruvate and ATP. It is an important metabolic pathway for energy production, but it is not the most rapid source of energy.

  D: Swine flu is caused by the Influenza virus and tourniquet test is not used in its daily follow-up.

  D: Swine flu is a respiratory disease caused by the influenza A virus, and it does not involve capillary fragility.
Action: Answer("B")
Response 2:
Knowledge: 
  The tourniquet test, also known as the Rumpel-Leede test, is used to detect capillary fragility. The test is done by inflating a blood pressure cuff on the arm to a point midway between the systolic and diastolic pressures for 5 minutes, and then releasing it. The test is positive if more than 20 petechiae (small red or purple spots caused by bleeding into the skin) per square inch develop within 5 minutes.
  A: Zika virus infection does not typically cause capillary fragility, and the tourniquet test is not used in patients with Zika virus.
  B: Dengue virus infection can cause capillary fragility, and the tourniquet test is commonly used in patients with dengue fever to help evaluate the risk of developing severe dengue.
  C: Chikungunya virus infection can cause capillary fragility, but the tourniquet test is not commonly used in patients with chikungunya.
  D: Swine flu (influenza A/H1N1) does not typically cause capillary fragility, and the tourniquet test is not used in patients with swine flu.
Action: Answer("B")

Choices:
  A: Langerhans cell histiocytosis
  B: Giant cell tumor
  C: Chondroblastoma
  D: Osteoid osteoma
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  Langerhans cell histiocytosis is a rare disorder that occurs when Langerhans cells, a type of white blood cell, build up in certain tissues such as bones and cause damage.
  Giant cell tumor (GCT) is a benign tumor which typically occurs in the distal femur, proximal tibia, or distal radius.
  Chondroblastoma is a rare type of non-cancerous bone tumor that begins in cartilage.
  Osteoid osteoma is a benign bone tumor that usually affects young adults.

Action: Answer("B")  
Based on the description of the presentation and the X-ray findings, the most likely diagnosis is giant cell tumor (choice B).
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  Langerhans cell histiocytosis (LCH) is a condition characterized by proliferation of Langerhans cells in different organs including bones.
  Giant cell tumor (GCT) is a benign tumor composed of osteoclast-like giant cells and spindle-shaped stromal cells.
  Chondroblastoma is a rare, benign cartilaginous neoplasm arising from chondroblasts.
  Osteoid osteoma is a benign skeletal tumor that typically affects young individuals and is characterized by a central nidus of mineralized tissue.
  Lytic lesions in bones with young individuals encompass a wide range of differential diagnoses. 
  Grooved nuclei, giant cells eosinophilic cytoplasm and fibroblastic proliferation are characteristic of Giant cell tumor.

  GCT is a benign bone tumor that arises in the epiphysis or metaphysis of long bones. GCT consists of multinucleated giant cells, stromal cells, and mononuclear cells.
  CB is a rare benign bone tumor that occurs most frequently in the epiphysis or apophysis of long bones. These tumors occur in the young, usually below the age of 20 years.

Clay-colored stools are suggestive of hepatobiliary disease, which narrows down the possible causes of neonatal jaundice. Giant cells found on liver biopsy suggest a viral or autoimmune etiology.

This choice seems plausible as clay-colored stools suggest biliary obstruction. Extrahepatic biliary atresia is a correct diagnosis in this scenario, and liver biopsy with giant cells is common in this condition.

C: Physiological jaundice.
This choice would be incorrect as clay-colored stools suggest hepatobiliary disease, which is not a feature of physiological jaundice.

D: Physiological jaundice with extrahepatic biliary atresia.
This choice is unlikely as extrahepatic biliary atresia is not a feature of physiological jaundice.

  B: Ferrochelatase adds iron to protoporphyrin IX to form heme. Deficiency in ferrochelatase causes erythropoietic protoporphyria (EPP). But this is not related to lead poisoning.
  C: Porphobilinogen accumulates in acute intermittent porphyria (AIP). But its accumulation is not related to lead poisoning.
  D: Delta amino levulinic acid (ALA) accumulates in the blood and urine due to inhibition of ALA dehydratase and ferrochelatase by lead in lead poisoning.
Action: Answer("D")

These two enzymes are at different points in the heme biosynthetic pathway.

  C: Porphobinogen is a precursor of heme that is formed from delta-aminolevulinic acid.

  B: Repaglinide is a meglitinide, which requires a dose adjustment in renal impairment. It is also administered orally.
  C: Vildagliptin is a DPP-4 inhibitor, which requires dose adjustments in renal impairment. It is also administered orally.
  D: Glimepiride is a sulfonylurea, which requires dose adjustments in renal impairment. It is also administered orally.

Response 1:
Knowledge: 
  Stage 5 chronic kidney disease results in significant loss of renal function, which leads to altered pharmacokinetics of certain medications.
  A: Linagliptin is a dipeptidyl peptidase-4 (DDP-4) inhibitor, which undergoes enterohepatic cycling and predominantly excreted in feces. It doesn't require any dose adjustment in the setting of chronic kidney disease. However, it may be less effective with an estimated glomerular filtration rate (eGFR) less than 30 ml/min/1.73 m².
  B: Repaglinide is a meglitinide secretagogue, which is metabolized in the liver and primarily excreted in feces. It doesn't require any dose adjustment in the setting of chronic kidney disease.
  C: Vildagliptin is a DDP-4 inhibitor, which undergoes hepatic metabolism and predominantly excreted in urine. It requires dose adjustment in the setting of chronic kidney disease.
  D: Glimepiride is a sulfonylurea secretagogue, which is metabolized in the liver and primarily excreted in urine. It requires dose adjustment in the setting of chronic kidney disease.

Knowledge:

  B: Repaglinide is an oral medication for type 2 diabetes that stimulates insulin release from the pancreas and is mainly metabolized by the liver. It does not require dose modification in renal failure.
  C: Vildagliptin is an oral medication for type 2 diabetes that works by increasing incretin hormones and has a renal clearance of 24%, so it requires dose modification in renal failure.
  D: Glimepiride is an oral medication for type 2 diabetes that stimulates insulin release from the pancreas and undergoes hepatic metabolism, but it also requires dose modification in renal failure.

Topic: Social & Preventive Medicine
Question: Which of the following is used for selecting patients with respect to potential factors that will affect the results?
Choices:
  A: Systematic random sampling
  B: Simple random sampling
  C: Stratified random sampling
  D: Cluster sampling
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  A: Systematic random sampling involves selecting every kth participant from a list of the population. 
  B: Simple random sampling involves selecting participants randomly from the population. 
  C: Stratified random sampling involves dividing the population into subgroups and then randomly selecting participants from each subgroup.
  D: Cluster sampling involves dividing the population into clusters and randomly selecting some of the clusters and then selecting all participants in the selected clusters.

Answer: C
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  A: Systematic random sampling is a sampling method where the elements or individuals are selected from an ordered sampling frame at a fixed interval.
  B: Simple random sampling is a sampling method where each member of the population has an equal chance of being selected, and each sample of the same size has an equal chance of being selected from the population.
  C: Stratified random sampling is a sampling method where the population is divided into subgroups or strata, and members are randomly selected from each stratum in proportion to the size of the stratum.
  D: Cluster sampling is a sampling method where the population is divided into clusters or groups, and a random sample of clusters is selected. 

Answer: C
Response 2:
Knowledge:
  A: Systematic random sampling is a method where every nth person is included in the study starting from a random person.
  B: Simple random sampling is a method where every person has an equal opportunity to be included in the study.
  C: Stratified random sampling is a method where the population is divided into sub-groups and then random sampling is carried out from each sub-group.
  D: Cluster sampling is a method where groups of individuals are randomly selected and all individuals within those groups are included in the study.
  
Answer: C
Response 3:
Knowledge:
  A: Systematic random sampling is a method of selecting a random sample from a larger population. The selection of each subject in the population is based on a predetermined mathematical formula.
  B: Simple random sampling is a method of selecting a random sample from a larger population by giving each member of the population an equal chance of being selected.
  C: Stratified random sampling is a method of selecting a random sample from a larger population that is subdivided into strata. Members of each stratum are selected randomly and in proportion to the size of the stratum. This method is used to ensure that the sample is representative of the population with respect to different subgroups.
